I took my 2008 Range Rover Land Rover Supercharged in for service and to have a oil leak and tire pressure light checked out. The rep pulled up the VIN# and began asking me questions pertaining to the cars history. He began asking where did I buy the car, and  who completed the last oil change? He then goes on to say that there was a recall on the vehicle (faulty air bag) that hadn't been fixed. I explained to him that the recall repair was completed by Range Rover Rocklin a little over a month from the time he checked it. According to him they hadn't put it in the system to show it was cleared. He then goes on to say if I wanted his service people to check out my car it would cost $195.00 to diagnose each area and that's not included in the work had I got it done! He then says I want your business but it might be better off if you took your car to the shop who last done the work. I took my car to the dealership  trusting that they could fix the problem better than a non range rover certified mechanic.  I feel this rep saw me as being a black man driving a nice vehicle and wanted to price gauge me. I would be curious to know what other people have been
charged for a diagnosis, yet how many other black persons have been treated the same...< /text>

<pics>None<//pics><Response>None</Response><gmapID>0x80c2d532c6fa00c7:0x64bd3ca34ed6d65d<//gmapID></record></dataset><record>
<Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPdwYlXNmA-T-ttrrSbKVsuu-8Pt2ecytdd0wef=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPom-VcFXC_-vuDFuO3Rz_2jux0bm_byfSmUw1L=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//Pics>< time>

<Review>First thing to note right now is that they're thankfully still open and running business as usual, however they're just not offering in-house dining just yet. You can order over the phone or walk in for takeout.

The bagels all look heavenly, along with their fresh juices, homemade cream cheese spreads, teas and vietnamese coffees. We ordered 2 sandwiches from their list of most popular options. Lox was my go-to of course and it absolutely didn't disappoint. The number of capers on it was a bit of overkill in my opinion, but it was great nonetheless. My fiance ordered the turkey, bacon, cheese and tomato on a jalapeno bagel. I had to have a bite because I can't turn my head from all things jalapeno. So so good!

We wanted some souvenirs to-go, so we obviously ordered half a dozen bagels, specialty cream cheese, and a vietnamese coffee for the road. This consisted of 3 gourmet bagels, hawaiian, sundried tomato, and spinach parmesan bagels paired with an 8 oz. container of homemade garlic herb cream cheese spread.

I actually dropped my vietnamese coffee on the floor on the way out because I'm a huge klutz and went to clean it up but the lovely employees (I'm thinking the owner is the one who actually was interacting with us-- VERY friendly man) said to not worry about it. He mopped it up and poured me a fresh iced vietnamese coffee which I was very thankful for. Great hospitality and a kind attitude goes a very long way in the food industry. If your personality is beautiful and contagious, then that's a reason to come back in itself.

< review>
This place is a gem. They are located in Gardena but totally worth the drive. The cakes are amazingly delicious, very delicate, the texture is very light and not loaded with sugar. It's a small business which means every cake is carefully  crafted. And if you are wondering, yes, they do have parking  on site.< /review>

The best strawberry shortcake I have ever eaten in my life! The service was impeccable and they even included a few candles along with a nice personalized birthday decoration on the cake made of high quality white chocolate. I called ahead and the guy said he would hold the cake for me (I know they sellout frequently) and when I got there he had boxed it and had it waiting in the fridge for me. Awesome!!! I have to go back this week to try some of the other cakes and pastries that I saw were presliced in individual servings. I highly recommend trying out this place.< /Review>

<Text>The Oxnard Transit Center does show its age, but it has aged gracefully. There's lots of seating inside, the property is well maintained, there's a public lavatory of reasonable cleanliness, and the staff is friendly. There's a coffee shop that sells basic snacks and drinks. There's little hustle and bustle these days except when a small clutch of travellers arrive or depart on the trains. The transit center has not been immune to the wave of vagrants that roam the streets in the last few years, but on-site security has kept them at bay for the most part.</Text><pictures>None< /pictures><Response>None</Response>< Gmap_id>

< Review>
I was unsatisfied with my visit to Big Brand Tire. I had a small screw stuck in my tire that caused a slow leak. The screw was less than 1/4'' in diameter. The screw was towards the center of the tire (not near the shoulder and not on the sidewall).

The attendant - who was very nice and seemed competent - told me that it was impossible to fix and that I needed four new tires (this was for a AWD car), for about $600. The tires were all new and less than 3 months old so I was reluctant to spend that much money on new tires.

I left Big Brand Tires and went to a different shop who just looked at the tire, told me "no problem" and fixed it for $20 in like 15 minutes.

<Rating>4<//Rating><Resp>None<//Resp>< Review>
For over the years this has always been a great place to eat and to shop to honor local local businesses within a strip mall . We need more parking please more parking! The baby boomers such as myself need more handicap parking spaces. I have two hip replacements and my wife has one hip replacement. Need I say more? Other than that I hope and pray that the owners and management decide to develop some type of new parking spaces, even if they have to close down for a little bit and expand the parking overnight or a couple of days if necessary. Besides of this parking lot was suitable for residence I would say at least 10 years ago but now because of our booming economy, millennials and the frequent addition of new foreigners coming in from overseas and such at such a rapid pace that now we need to have more parking and disabled parking. This is the new reality and this is the new normal. It's not going to fix itself. Hopefully by this coming up fall that this can be fixed within this year or so. If not, all that tells me that this management or owners probably don't care, and all they care about is the money. I'm hope I'm wrong.</Review>
